## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration (dv_dt) depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t. The acceleration encodes restoring forces (functions of x), damping (functions of v), and potential external driving (functions of t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (with periodic driving)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing equation)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping with cubic position: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v * x**2 (coupled nonlinear terms)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Position-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v (multiplicative coupling)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (time-modulated stiffness)
- General polynomial restoring + nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v**3 + c4 * cos(c5 * t) (comprehensive nonlinear oscillator)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) → symmetric potential wells preserving oscillator symmetry
- Even-power position terms (x**2) → asymmetric potential indicating broken symmetry in the oscillator
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v → energy dissipation or injection (damping/anti-damping)
- Terms like (1 - x**2)*v → amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of self-sustained oscillations (limit cycles)
- Cubic position term x**3 with same/opposite sign as linear term → hardening/softening spring nonlinearity
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) → external periodic driving force causing resonance phenomena
- Product terms x*v → velocity-dependent force modulated by position, indicating non-conservative coupling
- Odd powers of velocity (v, v**3) preserve time-reversal dissipation structure; even powers (v**2) break it
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system where phase portrait fully characterizes dynamics
- sin(c*x) restoring force → periodic potential landscape (pendulum-type systems with multiple equilibria)

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT:

**GT:** `-0.0892*v³ - 0.7253*v*(1 - x²) - 1.4474*x - 1.4474*x*exp(-|x|)`

Expanding: `-0.0892*v³ - 0.7253*v + 0.7253*v*x² - 1.4474*x - 1.4474*x*exp(-|x|)`

So the GT has terms: `c_a*x + c_b*v + c_c*v*x² + c_d*v³ + c_e*x*exp(-|x|)`

The critical term is `x*exp(-|x|)`. Since this involves `|x|`, I need to find candidates that can reproduce this. Note that `exp(-|x|)` is NOT the same as `exp(-x)` or `exp(c*x²)` since `|x|` is not differentiable at 0 and behaves differently for positive vs negative x.

**Key question:** Can `x*exp(c*x²)` approximate `x*exp(-|x|)`? No — these are fundamentally different functions. `exp(-|x|)` is not equal to `exp(c*x²)` for any constant c. They have different functional forms.

Can `x/(c*x² + 1)` approximate `x*exp(-|x|)`? No — rational functions cannot equal exponential decay functions.

Can polynomial terms (x³, x⁵, x⁷, ...) in Taylor series match `x*exp(-|x|)`? The Taylor series of `x*exp(-|x|)` around x=0 involves `|x|`, making it non-analytic. For x > 0: `x*exp(-x) = x - x² + x³/2 - ...` and for x < 0: `x*exp(x) = x + x² + x³/2 + ...`. The function `x*exp(-|x|)` is an **odd function** (since `(-x)*exp(-|-x|) = -x*exp(-|x|)`), but its Taylor-like expansion has even-powered terms with sign changes. No finite polynomial can match it exactly.

**However**, the problem asks for **mathematical equivalence**, not approximation. So I need exact matches only.

The GT contains `x*exp(-|x|)`. None of the candidates have `exp(-|x|)` or `exp(-Abs(x))`. 

Let me check candidates with `exp(c*x²)` terms (candidates 1, 13-36, 40, etc.): Setting `c7` negative in `x*exp(c7*x²)` gives `x*exp(-a*x²)`, which is a Gaussian-modulated term, NOT equivalent to `x*exp(-|x|)`.

Candidates with `x/(c*x²+1)`: This is a rational function, not equivalent.

Candidates with `sin` or `cos` of `t`: These introduce time dependence not in the GT.

Candidates with `v*exp(c*x²)` (like 8, 19, 50): The `v*exp(c*x²)` term could potentially absorb `v*x²` terms via Taylor expansion, but cannot produce the `x*exp(-|x|)` term.

**Critical observation:** The term `x*exp(-|x|)` cannot be represented by ANY of the functional forms available in the candidates:
- `x*exp(c*x²)` ≠ `x*exp(-|x|)` for any c
- `x/(c*x²+1)` ≠ `x*exp(-|x|)`
- Polynomials in x cannot equal `x*exp(-|x|)`
- Trigonometric terms in t are irrelevant

No candidate can exactly reproduce the `x*exp(-|x|)` term, and this term has coefficient -1.4474 which is significant and cannot be set to zero.

Wait — but I should reconsider: could the `x*exp(-|x|)` term potentially be absorbed if there are enough polynomial terms to represent it? No, because polynomials cannot equal exponential functions over all x.

None of the candidates contain `exp(-|x|)` or any absolute value of x in an exponent. The only exponential-of-x terms are `exp(c*x²)`, which is fundamentally different from `exp(-|x|)`.

Therefore, no candidate can be made mathematically equivalent to the GT.

4. `x` (coefficient ≈ -1.4474)
5. `x*exp(-|x|)` (coefficient ≈ -1.4474)

The key challenge is matching `x*exp(-|x|)`. Since x takes both signs, `|x|` cannot be simplified.

**Can `x*exp(c*x²)` match `x*exp(-|x|)`?** No — `exp(c*x²)` is an even function of x (like exp(-|x|)), but `c*x²` vs `-|x|` are fundamentally different functions. They cannot be equal for all x.

**Can `x/(c*x²+1)` match `x*exp(-|x|)`?** No — a rational function cannot equal an exponential function for all x.

**Can polynomial terms (x³, x⁵, x⁷, x⁹) approximate `x*exp(-|x|)`?** The Taylor series of `exp(-|x|)` involves `|x|` which is non-analytic at 0. A finite polynomial cannot exactly equal `x*exp(-|x|)` for all x.

**Can `sin` or `cos` terms help?** No — trigonometric functions are linearly independent from exponentials of |x|.

**Can `exp(c*cos(c*x))` help?** No.

**Can `v*exp(c*x²)` help?** No — this has a `v` factor, not matching `x*exp(-|x|)`.

None of the candidates contain `x*exp(-|x|)` or `x*exp(-abs(x))` as a basis function. Let me verify each candidate type:

- Candidates with `x*exp(c*x²)`: This is `x*exp(c*x²)` which equals `x*exp(-|x|)` only if `c*x² = -|x|`, i.e., `c*|x| = -1` for all x ≠ 0. Impossible since the left side varies with x.

- Candidates with `x/(c*x²+1)`: Rational function, cannot match exponential.

- Candidates with polynomial tails (x³, x⁵, x⁷...): Cannot match non-analytic `exp(-|x|)`.

- Candidates with `sin`/`cos` of `t`: Can set coefficient to 0, but still need to match `x*exp(-|x|)`.

Since **no candidate** contains a basis function that can exactly reproduce `x*exp(-|x|)`, and this term cannot be zero (its coefficient is -1.44736), **no candidate matches**.

Let me double-check: could any combination of the available terms somehow produce `x*exp(-|x|)`? The available non-polynomial, non-v terms are: `x*exp(c*x²)`, `x/(c*x²+1)`, `x*sin(...)`, `x*cos(...)`, `exp(c*cos(c*x))`. None of these equal `x*exp(-|x|)` for any constant choices, as they have fundamentally different functional forms.
